# 1001x | Aster

[1001xarrow-up-right](https://www.asterdex.com/en/futures/BTCUSD)
 Mode offers a streamlined, fully onchain perp trading experience with up to 1001x leverage, eliminating the need for deposits. It supports select pairs on both BNB Chain and Arbitrum networks.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x#what-is-1001x)

**What is 1001x?**

1001x utilizes the ALP liquidity pool to provide liquidity across the supported trading pairs. By minting ALP, you contribute assets to the pool, effectively participating in market-making. This mechanism ensures deep liquidity and efficient trade execution.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x#key-features)

**Key Features**

**Onchain perp trading:** Trade perpetual contracts with high leverage. All transactions are recorded onchain.

**High leverage:** Access leverage up to 1001x for BTCUSD, amplifying your trading potential.

**Hedging strategies:** Implement techniques like delta-neutral strategies to manage risk and exposure effectively.

**Robust price oracles:** Price feeds are sourced from Pyth Network, Chainlink, and Binance Oracle, ensuring accurate and tamper-resistant pricing.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x#dumb-mode)

**Dumb Mode**

Dumb Mode is a unique feature designed for price prediction. It allows you to forecast minute-by-minute price movements. This mode is available on both BNB Chain and Arbitrum networks, offering an engaging way to test the market.

# Dynamic Fee for Degen Mode | Aster

Aster has introduced a dynamic fee model for Degen Mode, designed to tie closing fees to your position's PnL and protect users from losses.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/degen-mode/dynamic-fee-for-degen-mode#how-it-works)

**How It Works**

The closing fee rate is calculated using three inputs: the position's profit or loss, the notional value, and a minimum floor rate.

closeFeeRate\=max⁡(pnl⋅shareRatenotinal,closeMinRate)\\text{closeFeeRate} = \\max \\left( \\frac{\\text{pnl} \\cdot \\text{shareRate}}{\\text{notinal}}, \\text{closeMinRate} \\right)closeFeeRate\=max(notinalpnl⋅shareRate​,closeMinRate)

Where:

*   **PnL** is the profit or loss on the position
    
*   **shareRate** is the percentage of the notional value charged as a fee
    
*   **notional** is the total value used to open the position
    
*   **closeMinRate** is the minimum closing fee rate: the lowest fee that can be applied when closing a position
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/degen-mode/dynamic-fee-for-degen-mode#parameters)

Parameters

*   shareRate: 15% (default)
    
*   closeMinRate: 0.03% (initial)
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/degen-mode/dynamic-fee-for-degen-mode#example)

**Example**

For a position with $100 in profit, a 15% share rate, and a $600 notional:

Closing fee rate = Max(100 × 15% / 600, 0.03%) = 0.03%

In this case, the minimum closing fee rate of 0.03% applies.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/degen-mode/dynamic-fee-for-degen-mode#execution-fee)

**Execution Fee**

The execution fee is charged only when opening a position. It is set at $0.50 (BNB Chain) or $0.20 (Arbitrum), consistent with the fee charged on standard perpetuals trades.

[PreviousDegen Modechevron-left](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/degen-mode)
[NextDumb Modechevron-right](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/dumb-mode)

Last updated 23 days ago

# Deposit & Withdrawal Guide | Aster

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/spot/deposit-and-withdrawal-guide#depositing-funds)

**Depositing Funds**

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/spot/deposit-and-withdrawal-guide#option-a-deposit-from-a-cex)

**Option A: Deposit from a CEX**

1.  Log in to your CEX account (e.g. Binance, OKX).
    
2.  Go to Withdraw, select your token, and choose the correct network (e.g. USDT on BEP-20).
    
3.  Copy your Aster Spot deposit address. You'll find this in the Aster app or web under Account → Deposit.
    
4.  Paste the address into the CEX withdrawal page.
    
5.  Enter the amount and confirm.
    

Your funds should arrive in your Aster Spot account within a few minutes.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/spot/deposit-and-withdrawal-guide#option-b-deposit-from-an-on-chain-wallet-metamask-trust-wallet-etc)

**Option B: Deposit from an on-chain wallet (MetaMask, Trust Wallet, etc.)**

1.  Open your wallet and connect to the BSC network.
    
2.  Go to Send, select your token and network (e.g. USDT on BEP-20).
    
3.  Copy your Aster Spot deposit address. You'll find this in the Aster app or web under Account → Deposit.
    
4.  Paste the address, enter the amount, and confirm the transaction.
    

Once the transaction confirms on-chain, your funds will appear in your Aster Spot account.

_Always verify that both the network and the destination address are correct before confirming any transfer._

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/spot/deposit-and-withdrawal-guide#withdrawing-funds)

**Withdrawing Funds**

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/spot/deposit-and-withdrawal-guide#from-aster-spot-to-a-cex-or-wallet)

From Aster Spot to a CEX or wallet

1.  In the Aster app, go to Assets → Withdraw. On web, navigate to Perpetuals or Spot and click Withdraw under Account (bottom-right).
    
2.  Select your token.
    
3.  Enter the destination address (your CEX deposit address or on-chain wallet address).
    
4.  Enter the withdrawal amount and confirm.
    

Funds are sent on BSC and typically arrive within minutes, depending on network conditions.

_Always verify that both the network and the destination address are correct before confirming any transfer._

# Profit Share & Flat Fee | Aster

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/shield-mode/profit-share-and-flat-fee#more-fee-options)

**More Fee Options**

Aster has implemented a profit-sharing model to reduce the impact of fees on users. When the position is profitable, a fee range from 15% to 20% will be charged on the profits. When the position incurs a loss, no fees will be incurred.

For example, a 15% fee will be charged on the profits when you place orders on BTCUSDT or ETHUSDT pairs.

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FJ2WthTrrbRu09UmmKCso%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2026-02-09%252017.50.56.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Df5d84af4-5461-47e8-a3eb-e509bb655e94&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=ce0989ba&sv=2)

In the meantime, users can select the flat fee ratio when opening the position. 0.03% will be charged based on the notional value of the position.

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FlsosJjmBSLKfusDmdMk0%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2026-02-11%252009.54.31.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D1d3415ed-5a36-4fa3-b8f7-cebf9bf302fb&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=f0ca0e39&sv=2)

# Dynamic Slippage | Aster

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/shield-mode/dynamic-slippage#overview)

**Overview**

The Dynamic Slippage mechanism is designed to accurately reflect the market impact of user trades. Every order impacts market liquidity, particularly when the trade volume is large. To ensure fair pricing and risk management, slippage is calculated dynamically based on the order size, the current Open Interest (OI) imbalance, and real-time market depth.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/shield-mode/dynamic-slippage#calculation-logic)

**Calculation Logic**

The system determines the slippage percentage by comparing the calculated Market Impact against a configured Minimum Slippage threshold. The greater of the two values is applied.

**A. Long Scenario (Open Long / Close Short)**

This formula applies when a user opens a Long position or closes a Short position.

SlippageLong\=Max(NewPostion−SymbolShortOI+SymbolLongOI)/DepthAbove,MinLongSlippage)SlippageLong= Max{(NewPostion-Symbol Short OI+Symbol Long OI)/DepthAbove, MinLongSlippage)}SlippageLong\=Max(NewPostion−SymbolShortOI+SymbolLongOI)/DepthAbove,MinLongSlippage)

**B. Short Scenario (Open Short / Close Long)**

This formula applies when a user opens a Short position or closes a Long position.

SlippageShort\=Max(NewPostion−SymbolLongOI+SymbolShortOI)/DepthBelow,MinShortSlippage)SlippageShort=Max{(NewPostion-Symbol Long OI+Symbol Short OI)/DepthBelow, MinShortSlippage)}SlippageShort\=Max(NewPostion−SymbolLongOI+SymbolShortOI)/DepthBelow,MinShortSlippage)

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/shield-mode/dynamic-slippage#parameter-definitions)

**Parameter Definitions**

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/shield-mode/dynamic-slippage#market-depth-liquidity)

**Market Depth (Liquidity)**

Market depth data is aggregated from major exchanges via the CMC interface to determine the available liquidity for absorbing orders.

*   Data Sources: Binance, Coinbase, OKX, Kraken and other major exchanges (USDT or USD pairs).
    
*   Update Frequency: Every 5 seconds.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/shield-mode/dynamic-slippage#depth-formulas)

**Depth Formulas**

The depth values used in the denominator are calculated as follows:

**Depth Above (Ask Liquidity):**

Depthabove​\=k×100×∑(depthpositivetwo​)​Depthabove​=k×100×∑(depthpositive\_two​)​Depthabove​\=k×100×∑(depthpositivet​wo​)​

*   `_depth_positive_two_`_: Aggregated +2% depth data from sources._
    

**Depth Below (Bid Liquidity):**

Depthbelow​\=k×2100×∑(depthnegativetwo​)​Depthbelow​=k×2100×∑(depthnegative\_two​)​Depthbelow​\=k×2100×∑(depthnegativet​wo​)​

*   `_depth_negative_two_`_: Aggregated -2% depth data from sources._
    

**Adjustment Coefficient (k):** A scalar used to adjust liquidity sensitivity.

*   **Default:** k = 1.5
    
*   **Configuration:** Configurable per Symbol.
    

**Minimum Slippage:**

A fixed parameter configured at the Symbol level. This acts as a floor to ensure slippage never drops below a baseline value, even in high liquidity conditions.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/shield-mode/dynamic-slippage#precision-and-rounding-logic)

**Precision and Rounding Logic**

The final slippage percentage is processed with a precision of **1/10,000 (0.01%)**. The rounding method depends on which value is selected by the `MAX` function:

**Scenario A (Calculated Impact > Min Slippage):**

If the dynamic market impact calculation is higher than the minimum slippage, the system applies an **Unconditional Carry (Ceiling)** logic.

*   Action: Round **UP** to the nearest 1/10,000.
    

**Scenario B (Calculated Impact ≤ Min Slippage):**

If the minimum slippage is used, standard rounding applies.

*   Action: **Round Half Up (Nearest)** to 1/10,000.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/shield-mode/dynamic-slippage#example-logic)

**Example Logic:**

[PreviousForex Marketchevron-left](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/shield-mode/forex-market)
[NextLiquidationschevron-right](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/shield-mode/liquidations)

Last updated 24 days ago

*   [Overview](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/shield-mode/dynamic-slippage#overview)
    
*   [Calculation Logic](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/shield-mode/dynamic-slippage#calculation-logic)
    
*   [Parameter Definitions](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/shield-mode/dynamic-slippage#parameter-definitions)
    
*   [Precision and Rounding Logic](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/shield-mode/dynamic-slippage#precision-and-rounding-logic)
    

Copy

    // precision = 0.0001 # 1/10000
    
    if calculated_impact > min_slippage:
        # Unconditional carry (Ceiling)
        final_slippage = math.ceil(calculated_impact / precision) * precision
    else:
        # Standard rounding (Round Half Up) for Min Slippage
        final_slippage = round(min_slippage / precision) * precision

**Note:** The secret key is only shown once — immediately after creation. It cannot be retrieved again. If you lose it, delete the key and create a new one. Do not share either key with anyone.

**Additional limits and options:**

*   Each account supports up to 30 API keys.
    
*   Binding your API key to a fixed IP address is recommended for added security.

# Long/Short Grid Trading | Aster

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/grid-trading/long-short-grid-trading#what-is-long-short-grid-trading)

**What is Long/Short Grid Trading?**

Long/Short Grid combines a directional position with a grid trading system. You open an initial long or short position to express a market view, then layer buy and sell limit orders at regular intervals around the current price to capture volatility as the market moves.

The key difference from neutral grid: a long grid opens with an initial long position, a short grid opens with an initial short position. This lets you trade with a trend while the grid captures oscillations within your defined range.

**Example:** A trader bullish on BTC opens a long position in BTCUSDT, then places buy orders every $1,000 below the current price and sell orders every $1,000 above it — holding directional exposure while profiting from range movement.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/grid-trading/long-short-grid-trading#placing-a-long-short-grid-order)

**Placing a Long/Short Grid Order**

1.  On the grid trading panel, enter your strategy parameters:
    

Parameter

Description

**Upper Price**

Top boundary of the grid range.

**Lower Price**

Bottom boundary of the grid range.

**Number of Orders**

How many orders to place within the range.

**Grid Width**

The price interval between each order.

**Initial Margin**

Capital allocated to open and maintain the strategy.

**Note:** If the current market price is above your grid range when the strategy starts, it will launch with zero position.

1.  Set your initial margin. The system calculates the minimum required based on your grid count, leverage, and price range — denser grids require more margin.
    

**Note:** Each grid order must meet the minimum notional value requirement. If it doesn't, reduce the grid count or increase your initial margin. When margin falls below the minimum, the interface will display the exact amount needed to activate the strategy. Ensure your available balance and maintenance margin stay above the initial margin to avoid liquidation.

1.  Click **\[Create\]** to place the grid order.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/grid-trading/long-short-grid-trading#p-and-l-calculation)

**P&L Calculation**

Long/Short Grid P&L accounts for both matched (fully completed) and unmatched (partially completed) grid transactions.

Metric

Definition

Calculation

**Unmatched P&L**

P&L on incomplete grid pairs

(Latest price − unmatched pair's avg price) × unmatched volume

**Total Realized P&L**

Total realised profit/loss since launch

Matched grid income + unmatched P&L

**Yield (ROI)**

Total return on invested margin

Total profit ÷ initial margin × 100%

**Annualised Return (APR)**

ROI scaled to a yearly rate

ROI × (365 days ÷ days running)

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/grid-trading/long-short-grid-trading#advanced-settings)

**Advanced Settings**

**Trigger Price** — Set a price level at which the grid activates. The bot stays dormant until the market reaches your trigger, then begins placing orders based on your parameters.

**Stop Loss** — Define a price level outside your grid range. If the asset price breaches it, the entire grid position closes automatically, limiting downside if the market moves against the strategy.

**Monitoring and closing:**

*   Click **\[Active Grid\]** to view live grid details, order status, and P&L.
    
*   Click **\[Terminate\]** to close the grid strategy and all associated orders.
    

[PreviousAuto Grid Tradingchevron-left](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/grid-trading/auto-grid-trading)
[NextHedge Modechevron-right](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/hedge-mode)

Last updated 24 days ago

*   [What is Long/Short Grid Trading?](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/grid-trading/long-short-grid-trading#what-is-long-short-grid-trading)
    
*   [Placing a Long/Short Grid Order](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/grid-trading/long-short-grid-trading#placing-a-long-short-grid-order)

# Maintaining the Peg | Aster

USDF maintains its 1:1 peg with the US Dollar through multiple mechanisms: rigid redemption, arbitrage opportunities, and delta-neutral positioning. Together, these ensure price stability and minimize deviation from the intended value.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/maintaining-the-peg#id-1.-rigid-redemption-and-arbitrage-opportunities)

**1\. Rigid Redemption & Arbitrage Opportunities**

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/maintaining-the-peg#how-redemption-works)

**How Redemption Works**

USDF maintains a strict 1:1 redemption mechanism with USDT. You can redeem your USDF at any time for the equivalent value in USDT, ensuring a direct 1:1 correlation.

Example: If you hold 100 USDF, you can redeem it for 100 USDT.

The peg stays stable because the system guarantees there's always an equal amount of underlying assets (such as USDT) available for redemption. This creates confidence in the token's value.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/maintaining-the-peg#arbitrage-opportunities)

**Arbitrage Opportunities**

When the price of USDF deviates slightly from its 1:1 peg on liquidity pools or exchanges, market participants can profit by exploiting the discrepancy. This arbitrage activity naturally stabilizes the peg by bringing prices back into alignment.

Example: USDF Overvalued

Suppose USDF is trading at 1.02 USDT in a liquidity pool like PancakeSwap:

1.  Redeem 100 USDF at the fixed 1:1 rate → Get 100 USDT
    
2.  Swap the 100 USDT on PancakeSwap → Get 102 USDT worth of USDF
    
3.  Profit: 2% arbitrage gain
    

Example: USDF Undervalued

If USDF trades at 0.98 USDT:

1.  Purchase USDF at the discounted rate
    
2.  Redeem at the fixed 1:1 rate for USDT
    
3.  Capture the arbitrage profit when prices revert to peg
    

Arbitrage doesn't just benefit traders–it actively stabilizes price by reducing further deviation from the peg.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/maintaining-the-peg#id-2.-delta-neutral-positions)

**2\. Delta-Neutral Positions**

Beyond redemption, delta-neutral strategies provide additional price stability. By balancing long and short positions in underlying assets, the delta-neutral approach:

**Stabilizes Price**

Manages volatility of underlying assets (like USDT) to keep USDF's value consistently near 1:1 with the US Dollar, even during market fluctuations.

**Generates Consistent Yield**

Allows fee generation through liquidity mechanisms while minimizing exposure to volatile assets.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/maintaining-the-peg#id-3.-key-takeaways)

**3\. Key Takeaways**

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/maintaining-the-peg#id-1-1-redemption)

**1:1 Redemption**

USDF can always be redeemed at a fixed 1:1 rate for USDT, ensuring price stability and providing holders with a capital preservation mechanism.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/maintaining-the-peg#arbitrage-opportunities-1)

**Arbitrage Opportunities**

Market inefficiencies create natural profit opportunities that simultaneously stabilize the peg by eliminating price discrepancies.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/maintaining-the-peg#delta-neutral-hedging)

**Delta-Neutral Hedging**

Balanced long and short positions protect against volatility and maintain the 1:1 peg even during uncertain markets.

Together, these mechanisms ensure USDF remains stable and trustworthy as a value store within the Aster ecosystem.

# Liquidations | Aster

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/fees-and-specs/liquidations-1#understanding-liquidation-mechanics)

**Understanding Liquidation Mechanics**

Liquidation occurs when your account's margin balance is insufficient to cover the required maintenance margin for your open positions. When this happens, the system automatically closes your position to prevent your balance from going negative.

A forced liquidation is triggered when:

Margin = Initial Collateral + Realized PnL + Unrealized PnL < Maintenance margin​

To avoid liquidation (i.e., when the risk ratio hits 100%), it's recommended to keep your margin ratio below 80% by adding sufficient margin or reducing your position size.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/fees-and-specs/liquidations-1#how-liquidation-price-is-determined)

**How Liquidation Price is Determined**

Forced liquidation occurs when the Mark Price reaches the liquidation price. Aster uses the Mark Price to keep liquidations fair and minimize the impact of price manipulation.

*   In cross margin mode with hedge trading, both long and short positions of the same contract share the same liquidation price.
    
*   In isolated margin mode, long and short positions have separate liquidation prices based on the margin allocated to each.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/fees-and-specs/liquidations-1#what-is-maintenance-margin)

**What is Maintenance Margin?**

Maintenance Margin is the minimum amount of margin required to keep a position open. Different positions have different maintenance margin requirements. If your account margin ratio falls below the maintenance margin requirement, liquidation is triggered.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/fees-and-specs/liquidations-1#the-liquidation-process)

**The Liquidation Process**

When your account margin falls below the required maintenance level, Aster initiates a forced liquidation using a staged, priority-driven process that attempts to avoid full liquidation where possible.

**Step 1: Cancel open orders** All open orders tied to the affected account are immediately canceled to prevent new orders from affecting the liquidation flow.

**Step 2: Attempt position close with an IOC order** The system issues one large [Immediate-or-Cancel (IOC) orderarrow-up-right](https://docs.asterdex.com/product/asterex-pro/order-types#time-in-force-tif-options)
. The IOC fills as much as the market allows, and any unfilled portion is canceled. This step attempts to reduce the position size and eliminate the margin deficit without fully closing the position. **Step 3: Recheck margin** After the IOC executes, the engine recalculates your available margin accounting for realized losses and the liquidation fee. If the remaining assets meet the maintenance requirement, liquidation stops and your remaining position stays open. **Step 4: Bankruptcy and insurance fund takeover** If the IOC cannot fully eliminate the deficit, the leftover portion becomes a bankrupt position. That portion is closed at the bankruptcy price and transferred to the Insurance Fund, which covers losses arising from the bankrupt position to the extent possible.

**Step 5: Negative balance handling** If closing the bankrupt position still leaves the trader's balance negative, the insurance fund covers the shortfall if possible. If the insurance fund cannot fully cover losses, the system may trigger Auto-Deleveraging (ADL), in which profitable opposing positions are reduced to make up the deficit.

To avoid liquidation (i.e. when the risk ratio hits 100%), it's recommended to keep your margin ratio below 80% by adding sufficient margin or reducing your position size.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/fees-and-specs/liquidations-1#additional-notes)

**Additional notes**

*   **Smart Liquidation principle** The protocol uses a smart liquidation approach that prioritizes partial close via the IOC to avoid a full forced close when possible.
    
*   **Bankruptcy price** The bankrupt portion is closed at the bankruptcy price, which is the protocol price used to finalize the bankrupt position. Profits or remaining assets from handling bankrupt positions are retained by the insurance fund.
    
*   **Position size and margin tiering** Smaller positions often have less buffer and are more likely to be liquidated fully. Larger positions may receive more gradual, tiered liquidation treatment that helps avoid immediate full liquidation.
    
*   **Fees and recommendations** Liquidation involves realized loss plus a liquidation fee. To avoid forced liquidation and fees, close positions manually before you approach the maintenance margin threshold, reduce leverage, or add collateral.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/fees-and-specs/liquidations-1#liquidation-settlement-and-negative-balance-handling)

**Liquidation Settlement and Negative Balance Handling**

If your account ends up with a negative balance after liquidation, Aster may use funds from the insurance fund to cover the loss, but only under specific conditions.

To qualify for automatic settlement, all of the following must apply:

*   The negative balance is in a USDT perpetual account.
    
*   The account has no open positions (cross or isolated margin).
    
*   The negative balance does not exceed 5,000 USDT.
    
*   No funds have been transferred into the account after liquidation to offset the loss.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/fees-and-specs/liquidations-1#why-the-liquidation-price-keep-changing)

**Why the Liquidation Price Keep Changing**

The liquidation price is dynamic because it depends on your position and margin, any change in your total account equity will adjust the liquidation threshold automatically. You can refer to some key factors below:

*   Funding payments
    
*   Collateral value fluctuations
    
*   New positions opened or closed
    
*   Cross margin effects
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/fees-and-specs/liquidations-1#liquidation-fee)

**Liquidation Fee**

When your position is liquidated, a portion of the liquidation fee is allocated to the insurance fund (shown in your transaction history as "Insurance clear"). The fee is calculated based on the applicable liquidation fee rate and the notional value of the liquidated position.

Aster strongly encourages traders to manage leverage and margin carefully in order to avoid forced liquidation. In periods of extreme volatility, the insurance fund may be required to take over liquidation positions directly. When this happens, the takeover is executed at the bankruptcy price, which can be less favorable than the normal liquidation price and may result in greater loss for the trader.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/fees-and-specs/liquidations-1#additional-notes-1)

**Additional notes:**

*   Bankruptcy prices may fall outside the contract’s current market range.
    
*   Due to latency or syncing issues, some numerical values may update without notice.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/fees-and-specs/liquidations-1#how-cross-margin-affects-liquidation)

**How Cross Margin Affects Liquidation**

Aster uses cross margin by default. This means all your collateral and unrealized PnL from other positions help support your open trades.

This can reduce the chance of liquidation, but it also means all positions share the same risk pool.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/fees-and-specs/liquidations-1#does-leverage-directly-affect-liquidation-risk)

**Does Leverage Directly Affect Liquidation Risk?**

Yes. Higher leverage means a smaller buffer between your entry price and your liquidation price.

For example, a 50x position is much more likely to be liquidated than a 5x position because the room for price movement is very small.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/fees-and-specs/liquidations-1#what-happens-to-my-collateral-after-liquidation)

**What Happens to my Collateral After Liquidation?**

After your position is forcibly closed:

*   The system uses your collateral to cover losses
    
*   Any remaining collateral stays in your account
    

If losses exceed collateral, insurance funds or protocol buffers cover the difference.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/perpetuals/fees-and-specs/liquidations-1#how-to-reduce-liquidation-risk)

**How to Reduce Liquidation Risk**

*   Use lower leverage
    
*   Add more collateral
    
*   Set a stop loss
    
*   Monitor funding fees
    
*   Avoid oversized positions
    
*   Close positions before high-volatility events

# Order Types | Aster

In 1001x, the following order types are available:

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/order-types#market-order)

**Market Order**

A market order is a buy or sell order that is executed immediately at the best available price in the market.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/order-types#limit-order)

**Limit Order**

A limit order allows you to set a specific price at which you want to buy or sell. The order will only be executed if the market price reaches your specified limit price.

**Limit buy order:** Executed when the market price reaches or falls below your specified price.

**Limit sell order:** Executed when the market price reaches or rises above your specified price.

**Note:** There is no guarantee that a limit order will be filled.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/order-types#take-profit-order)

**Take Profit Order**

A take profit order is a type of limit order that closes an open position at a specified price to secure profits.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/order-types#stop-loss-order)

**Stop Loss Order**

A stop loss order is designed to limit potential losses by closing an open position at a specified price.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/order-types#important-considerations)

**Important Considerations**

**Fees:** Both an opening fee and an execution fee are charged when a position is opened. These fees are factored into the leverage amount.

**Order execution:** Trade orders may not be executed even if the target price is reached due to the following reasons:

*   **Mark price discrepancy:** The mark price, which is an aggregated price from various exchanges, did not reach the target price.
    
*   **Insufficient time at target price:** The target price was reached but did not remain at that level long enough for the order to be executed.
    

Order size exceeds available open interest: The total size of all open positions in that direction. Your order may not be filled if it's larger than what the market can support.

[PreviousManaging Positionschevron-left](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/managing-positions)
[NextDirect Contract Interactionchevron-right](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/direct-contract-interaction)

Last updated 23 days ago

# Price Oracles | Aster

1001x utilizes a robust and decentralized oracle system to provide accurate and real-time price feeds for trading pairs. This system aggregates data from multiple reputable sources to ensure price integrity and protect users from anomalies.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/price-oracles#data-sources)

**Data Sources**

*   **Primary source**: Pyth Oracle’s price feed serves as the anchor
    
*   **Verification**: Prices are cross-verified with Chainlink’s price feed
    
*   **Fallback**: For trading pairs not supported by Pyth Oracle, Binance Oracle is used as a backup
    

If Pyth Oracle’s price deviates by more than 1% from Chainlink’s price, a circuit breaker is triggered, causing the transaction to fail.

All trading pairs on 1001x use the oracle price of the listed assets as the index price.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/price-oracles#how-prices-are-fetched-and-verified)

**How Prices are Fetched and Verified**

1.  On-chain request: When a trader initiates a transaction, a request for the latest price is simultaneously triggered.
    
2.  Off-chain aggregation: Pyth Oracle retrieves the latest price and updates the index-weighted average price feed.
    
3.  On-chain verification: 1001x’s smart contracts compare Pyth’s price with Chainlink’s feed to verify data accuracy.
    
4.  Transaction completion: Once verification is successful, the trader’s transaction is executed.
    

This decentralized validation process ensures there is no single point of failure and typically completes within two blocks. Additional safeguards are in place to mitigate issues arising from market disruptions or connectivity problems.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/price-oracles#protective-measures)

**Protective Measures**

*   Single source deviation: If an exchange’s last price deviates more than 5% from the median price of all sources, its weight is set to zero in calculations.
    
*   Multiple sources deviation: If multiple exchanges show deviations greater than 5%, the median price of all sources is used as the index value instead of a weighted average.
    
*   Connectivity issues:
    
    *   If an exchange’s data feed is inaccessible but had trades updated in the last 10 seconds, the latest available price data is used for index calculation.
        
    *   If no trade data has been updated for 10 seconds, the exchange’s weight is set to zero in the weighted average calculation.
        
    

[PreviousDirect Contract Interactionchevron-left](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/direct-contract-interaction)
[NextSpotchevron-right](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/spot)

Last updated 23 days ago

# Overview | Aster

[**Aster Earn**arrow-up-right](https://www.asterdex.com/en/earn)
 is a yield-focused product within the Aster platform, giving users access to optimized DeFi and CeDeFi strategies with minimal friction. Rewards update in real time and are distributed automatically. There is no need to claim rewards manually and you can withdraw at any time.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/earn/overview#key-features)

**Key Features**

*   **High-yield strategies:** Earn returns through structured DeFi and CeDeFi opportunities.
    
*   **Secure custody:** Assets are safeguarded through partnerships with trusted custodians like Ceffu.
    
*   **asUSDF staking:** Stake USDF to receive asUSDF, a yield-bearing version of the stablecoin.
    
*   **Simple UX:** One-click staking makes it easy to participate.

# FAQs | Aster

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/faqs#what-is-usdf)

**What is USDF?**

USDF is a yield-bearing stablecoin minted with USDT. USDT and USDF are fully convertible at a 1:1 ratio on Aster.

Contract Address: 0x5A110fC00474038f6c02E89C707D638602EA44B5

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/faqs#what-are-usdfs-yield-sources)

**What are USDF's yield sources?**

Yield is generated through delta-neutral hedging strategies such as buying spot BTC, then placing a corresponding short for the same USD amount which earns funding rates.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/faqs#what-happens-to-my-usdt-when-i-mint-usdf)

**What happens to my USDT when I mint USDF?**

USDT is transferred to Aster's Ceffu account (our custodial partner). Ceffu then deploys the funds to create delta-neutral positions that back USDF and generate yield for asUSDF holders.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/faqs#what-is-usdf-smart-mint)

**What is USDF Smart Mint?**

USDF Smart Mint optimizes your USDT-to-USDF conversion rate by routing your mint through the best available path:

*   Direct mint on Aster adheres to a 1:1 ratio
    
*   PancakeSwap pools may offer better rates due to liquidity conditions
    
*   Smart Mint automatically chooses the path that gives you the best amount of USDF
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/faqs#what-is-the-minting-fee)

**What is the minting fee?**

Minting on Aster: No fee. If you use 1,000 USDT to mint , you receive 1,000 USDF.

Minting via PancakeSwap: A small swap fee applies. You'll see the estimated fee before confirming.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/faqs#how-do-i-redeem-usdf-for-usdt)

**How do I redeem USDF for USDT?**

You have two options:

Option 1: Redeem on Aster

1.  Go to the Redeem tab
    
2.  Enter your USDF amount
    
3.  Click \[Redeem\]
    
4.  Processing takes 1-2 days for standard amounts, up to 7 days for large amounts
    
5.  You won't earn Au Points during the waiting period
    
6.  Click \[Claim\] once processing is complete
    

Option 2: Swap on PancakeSwap

1.  Click \[Swap\]
    
2.  Receive USDT instantly (with swap fees)
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/faqs#what-is-the-redemption-fee)

**What is the redemption fee?**

Redemption on Aster: 0.1%. If you redeem 1,000 USDF, you receive 999 USDT.

Redemption via PancakeSwap: Swap fees apply. You'll see the exact fee before confirming.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/faqs#what-is-asusdf)

**What is asUSDF?**

asUSDF is an asToken on Aster Earn and the yield-bearing token of stablecoin USDF. To mint asUSDF, stake USDF on Aster Earn. Holding asUSDF allows you to earn additional rewards. The token contract is: 0x917AF46B3C3c6e1Bb7286B9F59637Fb7C65851Fb.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/faqs#how-is-asusdf-apy-generated)

**How is asUSDF APY generated?**

asUSDF APY is generated from delta-neutral strategies which also involve the collection of funding fees. APY is reflected in the net asset value of asUSDF.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/faqs#can-i-withdraw-my-asusdf-asusdf-to-usdf-at-any-time)

**Can I withdraw my asUSDF (asUSDF to USDF) at any time?**

Withdrawals will be subject to a T+1 hour waiting period (2 hours). Check your processing withdrawals in the \[Claim\] section.

Remember to click \[Claim\] after the waiting period ends.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/faqs#are-there-any-fees-involved)

**Are there any fees involved?**

There are no fees to mint or withdraw asUSDF.

[PreviousTutorialschevron-left](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/tutorials)
[NextUSDF and the Stablecoin Landscapechevron-right](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/usdf-and-the-stablecoin-landscape)

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/resources/media-kit#short-description)

Aster is a privacy-first perpetual futures exchange backed by YZi Labs, featuring innovations like Hidden Orders to shield user trading activity. It offers perpetual contracts across crypto, stocks and commodities, as well as crypto spot trading, and is powered by Aster Chain, a Layer 1 blockchain built to power the future of decentralized finance.

# Managing Positions | Aster

On 1001x, all positions are isolated. This means each position uses its own margin, and losses are limited to that position only.

You can track and adjust your open positions directly in the app.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/managing-positions#view-your-positions)

**View Your Positions**

The position panel displays all open positions associated with your connected address. Each row includes:

*   Trading pair (e.g. BTC/USD)
    
*   Position direction (long or short)
    
*   Position size
    
*   Entry price
    
*   Mark price
    
*   Liquidation price
    
*   Estimated PnL
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/managing-positions#close-a-position)

**Close a Position**

To close a position, click Close on the position row.

This will place a market order in the opposite direction of your current position and fully close it. For example:

*   A long position of 1 ETH will trigger a market sell of 1 ETH
    
*   A short position of 1 BTC will trigger a market buy of 1 BTC
    

You can also partially close a position by adjusting the order size before confirming.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/managing-positions#edit-margin)

**Edit Margin**

If your leverage is below 500×, you can add margin to your open position at any time by clicking on the "+" icon. This can reduce your liquidation risk.

Note: Adding margin is not supported for positions using 500× leverage or higher.

[PreviousDumb Modechevron-left](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/dumb-mode)
[NextOrder Typeschevron-right](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/order-types)

Last updated 23 days ago

*   [View Your Positions](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/managing-positions#view-your-positions)
    
*   [Close a Position](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/managing-positions#close-a-position)
    
*   [Edit Margin](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/managing-positions#edit-margin)

# VIP Program | Aster

**Note:** All maker fees for Aster perp trading were set to zero On February 2, 2026

**Note:** $ASTER holding requirements were added to the VIP Program on November 3, 2025

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/program-and-rewards/vip-program#overview)

Overview

The Aster VIP Program rewards our highest volume users by offering exclusive benefits and privileges.

VIP status is assessed daily at 23:59 UTC, based on two criteria that must both be met:

*   **Rolling 14-day trading volume** -- spot and perps volume (USD)
    
*   **$ASTER holding balance** — calculated as a daily average across your accounts
    

VIP members receive reduced taker fees for both spot and perps trading. Refer to the VIP tier table for specific volume thresholds and fee rates by level.

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252F7JjLpZA2iONvbUnbRqAK%252FAster%2520VIP%2520Program%2520Update%2520on%25202.25.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd8501b06-21b5-434a-8c48-244e0bd63957&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=22d52c50&sv=2)

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FbmRnvIqFiOOxwFavnCW1%252FAster%2520VIP%2520Program%2520Update.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D03cf26f0-1b0a-4d5a-85f2-91b71639862e&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=ad68edc5&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/program-and-rewards/vip-program#usdaster-holding-balance-calculation)

**$ASTER Holding Balance Calculation**

Your daily $ASTER balance is the combined average of holdings across your Spot account, Perpetual account and Aster Staking balance.

**Total Daily Average ASTER Balance = Daily Average Spot Balance + Daily Average Perpetual Balance**

Account

Calculation Method

**Spot**

Sum of hourly balance snapshots ÷ 24

**Perpetual**

Sum of hourly balance snapshots ÷ 24

**Aster Staking**

Sum of hourly balance snapshots ÷ 24

**Note:** Hourly snapshots occur at random times within each hour. Pending orders are included in the balance. Each day runs from 00:00:00 to 23:59:59 UTC.

# Aster Code | Aster

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/program-and-rewards/aster-code#what-is-aster-code)

**What is Aster Code?**

Aster Code is a broker ecosystem that lets builders collect fees when users trade through their custom interfaces. Builders create their own trading UIs on top of Aster's infrastructure and earn a commission on every executed trade routed through their interface.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/program-and-rewards/aster-code#how-aster-code-works)

**How Aster Code Works**

To become a builder and start earning fees:

1.  **Create an account:** Register using your Web3 wallet address.
    
2.  **Deposit the required amount:** Deposit a minimum of 100 $ASTER into your Aster perps account. The builder must maintain at least 100 $ASTER in their perps wallet throughout the process.
    
3.  **Build your UI:** Create your own trading interface and connect it to Aster Code. You can find the API demo code in the [Aster Code API documentationarrow-up-right](https://asterdex.github.io/aster-api-website/asterCode/integration-flow/)
    .
    
4.  **Invite users:** Users trade via your UI page. They must complete both Agent approval and Builder fee approval the first time they trade through your interface.
    

To view builder fee details: visit the [Aster Codearrow-up-right](https://www.asterdex.com/en/aster-code)
 page and click Builder Center for an overview of your fees and to claim them.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/program-and-rewards/aster-code#why-use-aster-code)

**Why Use Aster Code?**

*   **Fee collection:** Builders reliably earn a builder fee on executed trades (ADL and liquidation orders do not count toward builder fees).
    
*   **Transparent user consent:** Users explicitly approve both the broker (agent) and the maximum builder fee rate.
    
*   **Automated rewards:** Once an order is filled and validated, builder fees are recorded automatically on a daily basis.
    
*   **Simple integration:** The flow fits seamlessly into existing trading steps – users approve the builder and agent during the "Enable Trading" process.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/program-and-rewards/aster-code#api-documentation)

**API Documentation**

Full API documentation is available at: [https://asterdex.github.io/aster-api-website/asterCode/integration-flow/arrow-up-right](https://asterdex.github.io/aster-api-website/asterCode/integration-flow/)

[PreviousRocket Launchchevron-left](https://docs.asterdex.com/program-and-rewards/rocket-launch)
[NextPoints & Campaignschevron-right](https://docs.asterdex.com/program-and-rewards/points-and-campaigns)

# Dumb Mode | Aster

Dumb Mode is a forecast-based trading feature that lets users predict minute-by-minute price movements of an underlying asset. Trades settle based on the asset's entry and expiry prices.

Available on both BNB Chain and Arbitrum.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/dumb-mode#how-to-place-a-dumb-mode-order)

**How to Place a Dumb Mode Order**

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FdNpLtyoXjlBN4vGQbNdQ%252F%25E6%2588%25AA%25E5%25B1%258F2025-04-21%252016.04.08.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D7f35524c-44cc-463d-baac-1168db00290b&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c17bee81&sv=2)

Choosing the expiration period

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/dumb-mode#setting-the-expiration-period)

**Setting the Expiration Period**

1.  **Toggle to Dumb Mode.** Switch between Perp and Dumb modes and confirm you're in Dumb Mode.
    
2.  **Select your asset and expiration period.** Choose the asset you want to trade and set how long until the position expires.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/dumb-mode#available-expiration-windows)

**Available Expiration Windows**

For BTC/USD and ETH/USD:

*   5 minutes: Maximum ROI of 77%
    
*   15 minutes: Maximum ROI of 80%
    
*   30 minutes: Maximum ROI of 82%
    

For all other pairs:

*   30 minutes: Maximum ROI of 72%
    
*   1 hour: Maximum ROI of 77%
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/dumb-mode#opening-a-position)

**Opening a Position**

Choose a default percentage or enter the principal amount manually.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/dumb-mode#important-notes)

**Important Notes**

**Expiration timer:** The countdown starts when the transaction is confirmed on the blockchain, not when you click Long or Short.

**Entry price:** The price shown is for reference only. Your actual entry price is locked in at the moment the transaction confirms on-chain.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/dumb-mode#profit-and-loss-conditions)

**Profit and Loss Conditions**

**Long position**

*   If expiry price > entry price: you profit (subject to performance adjustments)
    
*   If expiry price ≤ entry price: you lose your entire principal
    

**Short position**

*   If expiry price < entry price: you profit (subject to performance adjustments)
    
*   If expiry price ≥ entry price: you lose your entire principal
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/dumb-mode#fees)

Fees

There are no open or close fees in Dumb Mode. A 6% fee on the principal applies to winning trades only, and is already factored into the displayed ROI figures.

[NextManaging Positionschevron-right](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/managing-positions)

# USDF and the Stablecoin Landscape | Aster

The stablecoin market has matured into a core layer of the crypto ecosystem. USDT and USDC dominate by volume but decentralized alternatives like DAI and Ethena's USDe have grown alongside DeFi. USDF sits in the decentralized category but with a different approach to yield and risk management. Below is a breakdown of how each compares.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/usdf-and-the-stablecoin-landscape#centralised-stablecoins-usdt-and-usdc)

**Centralised Stablecoins: USDT and USDC**

Both are pegged 1:1 to the US dollar and backed by fiat reserves held by centralized entities. Their main advantages are liquidity and widespread exchange and protocol support.

**USDT (Tether)** is the largest stablecoin by market cap and one of the most traded assets in crypto. Tether holds reserves in excess of its liabilities — $143.7B in assets against $136.6B in liabilities as of 2024 — and generated $13B in net profit that year. Revenue comes from interest on reserve assets (primarily government bonds) and transaction fees.

**USDC (Circle)** is positioned as the regulated, institutional-grade alternative. It exceeded $30B in market cap and processed $1T in on-chain volume in November 2024 alone. Circle generated $132.7M in on-chain revenue in December 2024, second only to Tether's $532.1M.

**Risks of centralised stablecoins:**

*   Counterparty risk — solvency and integrity of a single issuer
    
*   Reserve transparency — reliance on issuer disclosures
    
*   Regulatory exposure — subject to policy changes that can affect legality or value
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/usdf-and-the-stablecoin-landscape#decentralised-stablecoins-usde-and-dai)

**Decentralised Stablecoins: USDe and DAI**

**USDe (Ethena)** is a synthetic stablecoin that maintains its dollar peg through a delta-neutral hedging strategy using synthetic assets. It's composable with DeFi protocols and has historically offered up to 18% APY when converted to sUSDe. Revenue comes from liquidity provision, staking, and yield generation within its DeFi ecosystem.

**DAI (Sky)** is collateralised by a basket of cryptocurrencies held in onchain vaults (Collateralized Debt Positions). It's over-collateralized to absorb volatility and maintains its peg through smart contract mechanics on Ethereum. Sky generates revenue through stability fees and governance participation.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/usdf-and-the-stablecoin-landscape#usdes-bear-market-limitations)

**USDe's Bear Market Limitations**

USDF's yield model is closest to USDe's — but USDe has a structural weakness in bear markets. Its reliance on synthetic asset positions and perpetual funding rates means yield becomes unsustainable when funding rates turn negative for extended periods. Returns that look attractive in bull conditions can reverse sharply in downturns.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/usdf-and-the-stablecoin-landscape#how-usdf-compares)

How USDF Compares

USDT / USDC

USDe

DAI

USDF

**Type**

Centralised

Decentralised (synthetic)

Decentralised (collateralised)

Decentralised (multi-strategy)

**Peg mechanism**

Fiat reserves

Delta-neutral hedging

Over-collateralised vaults

Diversified DeFi strategies

**Yield**

None

Up to ~18% APY

Variable

Variable, with bear market diversification

**Bear market resilience**

Stable, no yield loss

Vulnerable to negative funding rates

Moderate

Designed to adapt via alternative strategies

**Counterparty risk**

Issuer-dependent

Protocol risk

Protocol risk

Protocol risk

**USDF's differentiation:** When funding rates turn negative or markets contract, USDF can shift toward alternative yield sources — such as DAI collateralised lending — to maintain returns without depending solely on perpetual market conditions. This multi-strategy approach is intended to provide more consistent yield across market cycles compared to single-mechanism models like USDe.

**Note:** USDF's underlying USDT reserves operate within a regulatory-compliant framework, which also positions it as a more viable option for institutional participants who require both decentralised mechanics and regulatory assurance.

# How USDF Works | Aster

USDF is a decentralized, yield-bearing stablecoin that combines innovative mechanisms for stability, risk management, and revenue generation. At its core is a low-risk delta-neutral strategy that powers consistent returns for holders.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/how-usdf-works#capital-flow-process)

**Capital Flow Process**

Minting USDF and deploying capital is a straightforward, transparent process:

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/how-usdf-works#step-1-mint-usdf)

**Step 1: Mint USDF**

Mint USDF directly with USDT (Tether) at a 1:1 ratio. For example, 100 USDT mints exactly 100 USDF. Once minted, the USDT capital enters a managed process designed to generate yield.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/how-usdf-works#step-2-transfer-to-ceffu-wallet)

**Step 2: Transfer to Ceffu Wallet**

The USDT is transferred to a Ceffu wallet, a custodial solution that securely holds the funds on behalf of Aster. The Ceffu wallet prepares the funds for deployment in yield-generating strategies and plays a critical role in fund management.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/how-usdf-works#step-3-open-positions-on-binance)

**Step 3: Open Positions on Binance**

Funds from the Ceffu wallet are sent to Binance to open carefully managed strategic positions. Binance is chosen for its liquidity, efficiency, and support for sophisticated trading strategies. Funds are deployed for low-risk trading and revenue-generating opportunities designed to provide consistent returns.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/how-usdf-works#step-4-weekly-profit-distribution)

**Step 4: Weekly Profit Distribution**

Profits generated from trading and strategies accumulate over the course of each week, where the yield is then calculated and distributed to the asUSDF contract. asUSDF is the staked version of USDF, allowing holders to lock their tokens and earn passive income over time.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/how-usdf-works#delta-neutral-strategy-for-revenue-generation)

**Delta-Neutral Strategy for Revenue Generation**

The core strategy powering USDF returns is delta-neutral positioning. This approach maintains stability and minimizes market volatility exposure while generating consistent rewards.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/how-usdf-works#what-is-a-delta-neutral-strategy)

**What Is a Delta-Neutral Strategy?**

A delta-neutral strategy involves holding both long and short positions simultaneously. The goal is to neutralize the effects of price movements regardless of market direction, and the overall position value remains relatively stable.

In USDF's case, funds may be used for perpetual trading on platforms like Binance. By carefully balancing long and short positions, the strategy generates profits through trading fees and cost differentials rather than relying on price appreciation.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/how-usdf-works#revenue-sources)

**Revenue Sources**

The delta-neutral strategy generates revenue from multiple sources:

**Trading Fees**

Exchanges like Binance charge fees for opening and closing positions. By employing a delta-neutral approach, USDF generates consistent fee income while reducing risk exposure.

**Interest Rate Differentials**

When leverage is involved in trading, USDF can benefit from interest rate differences between various crypto assets and trading pairs, generating additional income while maintaining market neutrality.

**Stable Returns**

Unlike directional strategies that depend on market movements in one direction, delta-neutral positioning provides stable returns even during uncertain or bearish market conditions. The system continues generating returns for holders regardless of whether assets are rising or falling.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/how-usdf-works#how-it-works-in-practice)

**How It Works in Practice**

Here's how the delta-neutral strategy operates for USDF:

1.  Funds deposited into Binance are used to simultaneously buy spot (long) and short perpetual positions on a specific asset like Bitcoin (BTC) or Ether (ETH)
    
2.  Spot purchases profit when asset prices increase
    
3.  Short positions profit when prices decrease
    
4.  Counterbalancing positions offset each other, keeping the net position close to neutral in terms of market exposure
    

This structure means USDF generates consistent fee income regardless of asset price movements. The strategy is less sensitive to market volatility, and any gains or losses are offset by the balanced positions, keeping USDF's value stable.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/how-usdf-works#summary)

**Summary**

USDF combines collateral security, strategic positioning, and passive income distribution to deliver a stablecoin that maintains its peg while rewarding holders with yield. The delta-neutral approach ensures returns in any market environment, making it a robust foundation for the Aster ecosystem.

[PreviousOverviewchevron-left](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview)
[NextMaintaining the Pegchevron-right](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/maintaining-the-peg)

Last updated 22 days ago

*   [Delta-Neutral Strategy for Revenue Generation](https://docs.asterdex.com/usdf-stablecoin/overview/how-usdf-works#delta-neutral-strategy-for-revenue-generation)

# Fees & Slippage | Aster

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FgBl72kb3DQq6Ssu96wFb%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D99b7d129-30dc-4b32-943c-842697ed8689&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=916aa8b1&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/fees-and-slippage#opening-position-fee)

**Opening Position Fee**

A 0.08% fee is charged when opening a position, calculated as:

> _Opening fee = Number of contracts × Entry price × Opening fee rate_

**Example**

If a trader on BNB Chain opens a 1 ETHUSD long position at $1,500:

> Opening fee = 1 × 1,500 × 0.08% = $1.20

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/fees-and-slippage#closing-position-fee)

**Closing Position Fee**

A 0.08% fee is also charged when closing a position, calculated as:

> _Closing fee = Number of contracts × Close price × Closing fee rate_

**Example**

If the same trader closes the 1 ETHUSD position at $1,600:

> _Closing fee = 1 × 1,600 × 0.08% = $1.28_

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/fees-and-slippage#dynamic-pnl-based-close-fee)

**Dynamic PnL-Based Close Fee**

For positions using 500×, 750×, or 1001× leverage, no opening fee is charged. Instead, a dynamic closing fee is applied, calculated based on the realized PnL.

The minimum closing fee under this model is 0.03%.

![](https://apollox-finance.gitbook.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Flh5.googleusercontent.com%2Fx-j0hkF1yifTiEfpjNKi9QxklpcglxrspGw_zyq7T_x9jhm4amRlqWuVhID7Vc4g_ZRbTZSvgADb3SdkVDM7URENgpX-VTHzQO_ub3DjZkywItw1DA8WUk-x2_uxGOTrKLGdVRkbuN0Sp0Zwgygmi8c&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=afbf17f3&sv=2)

Where:

*   PnL = Profit or loss on the position
    
*   Share rate = Percentage of notional paid in fees (e.g. 15%)
    
*   Notional = Value used to open the position
    
*   Close min rate = Minimum fee rate applied (e.g. 0.03%)
    

Example

![](https://apollox-finance.gitbook.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Flh5.googleusercontent.com%2FJBltC7k0bpU6vJBnkwdmtndsWuXaY1ti1OMzqVeMkOmQMuaptZTTy7m2zve9BfsywU12w2Nylz4JVI033tzLicDAvbThaljCFFFxcj1apyL6vqmVBWTJroohNd8ShV6mB0LPrEeOO-sTIq4c6u_nq7Q&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=3589ca81&sv=2)

If the position has a $100 profit, share rate is 15%, and notional is $600:

> _Closing fee rate = Max((100 × 15%) / 600, 0.03%) = 0.03%_

**Note**: In the event of liquidation, the 85% liquid loss rate includes this closing fee.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/fees-and-slippage#execution-fee)

**Execution Fee**

This fee covers network costs and ensures smooth order execution. It is charged only when a position is opened.

*   BNB Chain: $0.50
    
*   Arbitrum: $0.20
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/fees-and-slippage#forex-perpetual-contracts-only-on-bnb-chain)

**Forex Perpetual Contracts (only on BNB Chain)**

![](https://docs.asterdex.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F4068247257-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FWhSHuKmgnGREbVb12PK2%252Fuploads%252FtJfp5G5EQfT4yvPDZ9s1%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D24e24bbf-f185-44f5-89a0-115ad8a999cd&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=9a38a383&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/fees-and-slippage#funding-rate)

**Funding Rate**

The funding rate helps balance long and short positions on 1001x. It protects the ALP from excessive risk exposure and reduces the pool’s exposure to large open positions.

Funding is calculated **every block**. When market conditions change, the accumulated funding fee is automatically updated. This fee is reflected in a position’s **unrealized PnL** and directly affects the **liquidation price**.

*   If the user holds a **long** position, the fee uses the **long funding rate**
    
*   If the user holds a **short** position, the fee uses the **short funding rate**
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/fees-and-slippage#funding-fee-formula)

**Funding Fee Formula**

> _Funding fee per block = (Number of contracts × Price) × Funding rate per block_

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/fees-and-slippage#funding-rate-per-block)

**Funding Rate Per Block**

The funding rate per block is determined by the gap between long and short open interest and the platform’s current borrow rate.

**When long positions > short positions:**

*   Long basic funding rate = -abs(funding rate p)
    
*   Short basic funding rate = abs(funding rate p)
    

**When short positions > long positions:**

*   Short basic funding rate = abs(funding rate p)
    
*   Long basic funding rate = -abs(funding rate p)
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/fees-and-slippage#final-funding-rate)

**Final Funding Rate**

*   Long funding rate = Long basic funding rate − Borrow rate
    
*   Short funding rate = Short basic funding rate − Borrow rate
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/fees-and-slippage#borrow-rate)

**Borrow Rate**

The borrow rate is reviewed and adjusted regularly as part of platform risk management. It is influenced by:

*   The size of the position
    
*   The time the position is held
    

![](https://apollox-finance.gitbook.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F86643275-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FKgTrH6FlpxEZKMS3bN7R%252Fuploads%252FdDz79MnN66rRRSHClfEm%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Da5ab0f83-828c-477c-96e9-3fcb3f9b7875&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b6d1c5cd&sv=2)

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/fees-and-slippage#base-interest-rate-per-block)

**Base Interest Rate Per Block**

The base interest rate per block is used to help calculate the borrow rate dynamically, based on recent market volatility.

> _Base interest rate per block = Base interest rate / (365 × 28,800)_

Where:

*   Base interest rate = k × HV
    
*   k = Adjustment factor (default: 1.25, platform adjustable)
    
*   HV = Historical volatility = 2-week average volatility × 365
    

This allows the platform to adjust borrow costs dynamically in response to volatility.

For more, see the historical volatility & base interest rate below:

![](https://apollox-finance.gitbook.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F86643275-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FKgTrH6FlpxEZKMS3bN7R%252Fuploads%252F8knme1A3VfJbsoVcN6d5%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D42a46633-36ef-4662-81dd-ffc78d61c474&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=cf88dfa1&sv=2)[119KBHV&BaseInterestRate.xlsxarrow-up-right](https://86643275-files.gitbook.io/~/files/v0/b/gitbook-x-prod.appspot.com/o/spaces%2FKgTrH6FlpxEZKMS3bN7R%2Fuploads%2FVyhBYUAEUAV7xKbA4Lx6%2FHV%26BaseInterestRate.xlsx?alt=media&token=20619efe-eee9-4793-baf4-33ebdc431f23)

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/fees-and-slippage#liquidation)

**Liquidation**

Liquidation occurs when a position’s mark price reaches its **liquidation price**. This price is determined by factors like leverage, margin, funding, and the platform’s liquidation loss rate.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/fees-and-slippage#liquidation-price-distance)

**Liquidation Price Distance**

The liquidation price distance is calculated as:

> _Liquidation price distance = Entry price × (Initial margin × Liquidation loss rate + Cum funding fee) / Initial margin / Leverage_

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/fees-and-slippage#liquidation-price-formulas)

**Liquidation Price Formulas**

For long positions:

> _Liquidation price = Entry price − Liquidation price distance_

For short positions:

> _Liquidation price = Entry price + Liquidation price distance_

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/fees-and-slippage#parameter-definitions)

**Parameter Definitions**

*   Entry price: The price at which the position is opened
    
*   Initial margin: The collateral the trader deposits to open the position
    
*   Liquidation loss rate: The default platform-defined loss factor during forced liquidation (default: 90%)
    
*   Cum funding fee: The total accumulated funding fees since the position was opened
    
*   Leverage: The leverage multiple selected by the user
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/fees-and-slippage#example)

Example

If a trader opens a long ETH/USD position at 10× leverage with:

*   Entry price: $1,500
    
*   Initial margin: $100
    
*   Funding fee: $2
    
*   Liquidation loss rate: 85%
    

Then:

> Liquidation price distance = 1,500 × (100 × 85% + 2) / 100 / 10
> 
> \= 1,500 × (85 + 2) / 1,000
> 
> \= 1,500 × 87 / 1,000
> 
> \= 130.5
> 
> Liquidation price = 1,500 − 130.5 = 1,369.5

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/fees-and-slippage#liquidation-1)

**Slippage**

Slippage on 1001x can be either **fixed** or **dynamic**, depending on the trading pair. The platform determines the slippage type based on the liquidity of the pair’s underlying assets, as observed from its oracle sources. This mechanism helps prevent price manipulation.

In general:

*   **Slippage increases** when open interest and new position size increase
    
*   **Slippage decreases** when oracle-source liquidity improves
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/fees-and-slippage#fixed-slippage-btc-eth-and-forex-pairs)

**Fixed slippage (BTC, ETH, and forex pairs)**

Fixed slippage is used for high-liquidity pairs like BTC/USD, ETH/USD, and forex contracts.

**Example:**

If a trader opens a long ETH/USD position when the Pyth oracle price is $1,500 and the slippage is 0.01%:

> _Entry price = 1,500 + (1,500 × 0.01%) = 1,500.15_

Because liquidity differs across trading pairs and source markets, slippage levels also vary by asset. In general, pairs with lower liquidity will experience wider spreads.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/fees-and-slippage#dynamic-slippage-all-other-trading-pairs)

**Dynamic Slippage (all other trading pairs)**

Dynamic slippage is used for trading pairs that don’t qualify for fixed slippage. It is calculated based on **ALP exposure**, current **open interest**, and the **size of the user’s new position**.

**Formulas:**

> _Long dynamic slippage (%) = (New position + Symbol long open interest) / 1% depth above_

> _Short dynamic slippage (%) = (New position + Symbol short open interest) / 1% depth below_

Where:

*   New position: Size of the user’s order
    
*   Long/short open interest: Current open interest for the symbol in each direction
    
*   1% depth above / below: Aggregated spot market depth within ±1% of the index price, based on major source markets
    

This design ensures that slippage scales with market impact and liquidity — helping maintain fairness and pool stability.

[NextDegen Modechevron-right](https://docs.asterdex.com/trading/1001x/degen-mode)

# Aster Convergence: Stage 6 | Aster

Just like in previous stages, Aster continues to use points as the core rewards mechanism for Stage 5. Points are calculated on a weekly basis, with each “epoch” running from Monday 00:00 UTC to Sunday 23:59 UTC, unless otherwise specified.

**What are points?**

Points are Aster Stage 6 Airdrop points for trading on Aster Perpetual and Spot.

**Scoring Formula:**

Final Points = (Trading points + Position Points + Aster Asset points +Liquidation points+ Profit and Loss Points) x Team boost + Referral points

**Note:**

*   Each category carries its own weighting to ensure balanced and fair rewards.
    
*   Adjustments may be applied to farmed points to maintain integrity.
    
*   Specific weightings and formulas remain undisclosed.
    

**Scoring Model Overview**

Points are calculated using a multi-dimensional scoring model, which considers multiple factors :

**Trading Points Score**

*   Trade Points are now calculated based on your trading fee contribution, liquidity (maker order) contribution and symbol boost factor.
    
*   Selected Spot and Perps symbols may boost your trading points.
    
*   Update hourly.
    

**Position Points Score - Only for Perpetual**

*   The larger size and longer time you hold a position, the more points you earn.
    
*   Points caps are not applied anymore on your trading volume.
    
*   Updated on a T+1 basis.
    

**Aster Assets Points Score - Only for Perpetual**

*   Earn points by using Aster assets such as $ASTER/asBNB/USDF as margin.
    
*   Points caps are not applied anymore on your used margin value to hold the positions.
    
*   Updated on a T+1 basis.
    

**Liquidation points - Only for Perpetual**

*   Liquidation points are generated when a position is liquidated.
    
*   The more liquidation fees a user generates, the more Liquidation Points they receive.
    
*   Update hourly.
    

**Profit and Loss Points Points Score - Only for Perpetual**

*   Hourly net profit and loss (excluding fees such as funding fees) contributes to points.
    
*   Updated hourly
    

**Team Boost & Referral Points Score**

*   Team boosts will accumulate throughout Stage 6.
    
*   and won’t reset during this period.
    
*   Team boosts for new members will take effect in a few hours after joining the team
    
*   Earn a share of your invitees’ based on the total points of your invitees and their invitees.
    
*   Points earned from first-level invitees are higher than those from second-level invitees. Updated daily.
    
*   Referral score example
    
*   A invites B, C, and D:
    
*   A earns from B/C/D’s base points (excluding team boosts).
    
*   If B invites C and C invites D (maximum two levels):
    
*   A also earns from C’s base points.
    

Base points include trading points score, positions points score, Aster asset holding score, and net PnL score.

**Note**

While the exact formulas and weightings remain undisclosed, all factors above are calculated weekly to determine your total points. These points accumulate toward your $ASTER airdrop share at the conclusion of Stage 6.

_**Terms & Conditions**_

*   Market Makers who are participating in the dedicated MM Program cannot earn points.
    
*   For each epoch, Aster may adjust the rules according to user feedback and market conditions.
    
*   Only participants who meet all the requirements will be considered as a qualified user.
    
*   The points are limited to only one entry per user; bulk registered accounts will not be eligible for rewards
    
*   Aster reserves the right to disqualify trades that are deemed to be wash trades, displaying attributes of market manipulation, bulk-account registrations to farm additional bonuses, or any other attempts at fraud.
    
*   Aster reserves the right to cancel or amend any Activity or Activity Rules at our sole discretion.
    
*   Aster reserves the right of final interpretation of this activity.
    

Risk warning: Crypto futures trading carries a substantial risk. All trading activities are done at your discretion and at your own risk. The information here should not be regarded as financial or investment advice from Aster. Aster will not be liable for any loss that might arise from your use of Aster.
